< Text>
Rancho basically has 3 donut shops within a 3 mile radius; this one, one on zinfandel and a third on sunrise/coloma.

This is my favorite donut shop. The donuts are like crispy kreme in the sense that the donut itself is light. But these have a bit more substance and bite vs crispy kreme. Super good and unique, I 100% recommend. Any of their glazed varieties are top notch, and their apple fritter isn't overly sweet.

Allen donuts is the smallest shop of ranchos 3 shop, but with the bestest donuts. The shop on sunrise is very good too. The shop's apple fritter is the best of the 3 shops, it's the least sweet. Their donuts are a bit above average for a donut shop. The donuts themselves have a good amount of substance, and isn't overly heavy. Friendly, I highly recommend this place.

The zinfandel shop is the worst of the 3. It's friendly, but the workers aren't as friendly as the other two. Their donuts have too much substance and are too heavy. This place produces safeway tasting/style donuts. Chewy, dense style donuts. Their apple fritter is dense, heavy, very very large and is way too sweet. The only thing I can recommend from this shop are their donut holes. This shop is also the most crowded and sometimes you'll encounter a local zombie coming down from their fix.<//Text>

<Review>DON'T WASTE YOUR TIME HERE.

I decided to check out the new Honda dealership since in the past I had to go out to Santa Monica or Irvine to check out new Honda motorcycles. Well, bottom line is, I will not be returning to this dealership. They wasted enough of my time today so I won't let them waste more by spending a long time on this review.

I stopped in on a Tuesday, spoke with the manager Mr. Cavenagh (Greg, I think) and said I was interested in trading in my 2012 Kawasaki Vulcan 900 Custom for a 2015 Honda Fury, he said that would be great and I could come in with my bike any day and do a test ride and they could check out the trade. So i came in 2 days later with my bike, the sales person, Eric, whom I had been dealing with on the phone earlier in the day setting up the demo ride with, came out, checked out the bike, said it was great and had me turn it on, rev, etc. So then we go talk numbers, they offer me a fair enough amount for my trade, we come to an agreement on price after about an hour, which includes the usual way over invoice markup and whatnot, and they had the classic bait and switch (listed for $1000 less on their website) and make it sound like they are doing me a big favor by honoring...their own price they had listed... SO, Then comes the test ride to make sure I enjoy the bike (I have 4 bikes at the moment and am very particular about what I want in a new bike)

Eric says he doesn't have a demo bike for the Fury so it will be about and hour while they set one up so I can demo it. After some more waiting he comes back and says that  I can only demo ride if its sold to me (not much of a demo...if I own it) and also, they did not want to take my bike as a trade because its a Kawasaki and they are Honda only and don't really have the ability to take a non-honda in a trade. THIS is what made me really angry, the whole time they knew what bike I was interested in trading. They knew damn well it was not a Honda, and it's in great condition so that wasn't an issue (garage kept, only 3k miles, etc) Good enough condition that after checking it out they had offered me a good enough trade in value for us to advance to the next hour or so of negotiation. He said it was management that was to blame, yet when i spoke to general manager originally and set it all up, it was no issue at all. Nor is it an issue at any other dealership, even brand exclusive ones. Also, I should mention they have used NON HONDA bikes already on their website listed under pre-owned inventory.

So they literally wasted about 3 hours of my only day off (not to mention some gas money going over there again) What really pisses me off is that they were about to run my credit for financing, knowing they were just going to not take the trade and still try to sell me the Fury. Hoping I would just buy it anyways?

I'm still interested in the Fury, so I guess I will have to drive out to Mission Motorsports in Irvine (They have a great staff and no BS) What a disappointment though.

<text>My wife surprised me with a stay at Cedar Gables Inn. It was my 50th birthday.
For starters when they became aware of my birthday we were upgraded to a bigger room.
I absolutely love history and old hotels. This place is amazing. The peace and quiet is incredible. What a stress reliever. If you need to decompress this is the place.

< text>
Stayed at Cedar Gable Inn on May 30 and 31, 2019

Pros

1. Excellent location as it is very close to downtown.  Like a 5 minute walk.

2. If you like rustic, historical buildings with a musty smell and creaky floors, this is the place for you.

3. Nicely updated bathrooms.

Cons

1. Absolutely no check-in desk or receptionist.  You must ring the door bell and wait for some staff member to open the door for you. Then they'll give you your room key and inform you of their policies.

2. If you need to ask a question or need something after 6 PM.  Good luck. There is no one to be found to help you.

3. Breakfast was almost inedible.  Ever had greasy pancakes with ham in it?

4. Security issues.
First our room had a single hung window which had no lock. Asked the owner about securing the window. He said that he couldn't      because the Inn is considered a historic building. Really, just for a window lock?
Second, all rooms had the old fashion locks with reusable keys which are easy to duplicate. No updating with electronic key        cards?

5. Yes, there is free parking on the premises as listed on their website, but there are only four spaces.  Better get there early                    otherwise, you must look for street parking.

Will not go back to Cedar Gable Inn.  Gave only two stars for the proximity to downtown.<//text>

The house is just amazing. Quaint garden in front and in back, guests are encouraged to explore. The house is furnished with antiques or reproduction (I can never tell), but I loved it anyways!
We stayed in Lady Margaret's room. The room was spacious with lots of storage for clothing for long stays, a fan, a fireplace, a jet tub, shower, and king bed. The bed was decent, a bit hard for me, but perfect for my husband.
You are given a key that accesses the front door, and your bedroom, for that added security.
Breakfast was delicious, and cooked as you are ready to sit the table.
Situated very close to "downtown" with so many restaurants, bars, shops, wine tasting venues, a pool hall, parks, etc.
We really enjoyed our stay, and will most likely book again!< /review>

For our first trip to Napa and being switched by Orbitz at last minute...we were pleasantly surprised.  The Cedar Gables is an older Inn that was built in 1892.  Neighborhood is filled with Victorian-type houses dome converted to Inns or BnB‚Äôs. Parking on street w/a couple of spots on grounds.  Has a lot of history and is well kept with large dining area, spacious kitchen, coffee & bar and TV viewing areas.  Very Victorian-ish in ‚Äòfeel‚Äô and atmosphere.  We stayed in room named Avon that faced the front of Inn.  Very small but clean room yet comfortable.  Bed was a little soft for my taste.  Breakfast was served daily between 8:30-9:30am. Guests were served fresh coffee and juice with a breakfast fruit and oatmeal appetizer then the breakfast entree all very tasty.  It gave you a chance to meet and talk with other guests.  Very nicely done by friendly staff.  Only a couple of blocks from old downtown and Napa river.  Some nice restaurants nearby as well.  Great jumping off spot for your visit to any of 500 wineries in Napa Valley!! Enjoy!!< /Review>

< review>
Cedar Gables is everything you ever dreamed a perfect B&B would be.  When you walk in the front door, you feel like you are walking into a dream of days gone by. Originally built in 1890, it has been updated with such authenticity and beauty that you want to search out every nook and cranny. And there is always a plate of delicious homemade cookies waiting for you on the living room table.  The inn keepers, Susie and Ken, were born to be doing what they are--making people happy and making sure every guest's wish is fulfilled. <review>So this is my first time trying this place, but my co-worker eats there once a week at least and offered to bring me some panang today when he picked up his. Yasssss hunty! I love me some panang so it was a no brainer for me. A couple of important things to note: 1) the panang has a kick to it. I'm a person that is a wimp but likes spicy anyway even though it makes me sweat a little. This was the perfect amount of spice for me! Enough to clear my sinuses but not so much that I was crying in pain. 2) I can be somewhat picky about veggies, and sometimes Thai restaurants use weird ones that I don't care for in curries. The panang just had chicken, potatoes, and a couple red bell peppers + Thai basil. Perfect for me! I love all those things! They do offer a veggie-only one, which I would imagine would make this vegetarian (probably vegan actually, as long as they don't use some sort of meat stock and/or dairy milk in it, but I believe it's coconut milk). Can't wait to try some of their other menu items! Will definitely be back!< /review><Pictures>None</Pictures>< Resp>

A small, pleasant restaurant with wonderful food. We have many similar choices in Sacramento and especially in the Broadway area and this is a stand out. Their lunchtime menu and especially the specials offer many more choices than elsewhere and not just the usual. I want to go back and try some new things.

Service fast and friendly. The restaurant is quiet and nicely decorated. The three of us had an unusually pleasant and agreeable lunch. Highly recommended.</Text>

< Text>
Came on a Saturday brunch with 2 others. Was steady flow of people, didn't make reservations but sat down where there were a few open tables. Service was subpar as it took at least 10 minutes to take our order and they forgot our drink order at the beginning when they sat us and had to pay at the counter before waiter came with our check (because it took so long and felt like they forgot us). Food presentation was good but was nothing extraordinary or exemplary - they got our special order correct on first attempt though! Sauces are spicy (good) and chorizo and chicken were okay. Main positive was no wait time (other than the wait for order) and staff were amicable.< /Text>

<Date>1618626715136</Date><rate>4</rate><review>First off I'd like to say... Puerto Azul is one of those places to go for Molcajetes and Mariscos. We did both today. My wife and I normally come to eat here for special occasions and it's always a nice atmosphere and terrific service. I'm posting several pictures today to show the beautiful presentation. The menu gives several items that are all delicious in my opinion. Today we went for an early supper and we tried a new item we've never had.. on the menu it's described as a pineapple filled with seafood. One ingredient that sort of killed the dish was an overwhelming amount of cheese all over the seafood inside the sweet pineapple. We also had some awesome azul oysters, queso con chorizo and a seafood Molcajete. We couldn't finish everything and asked to to go containers for our soon to be midnight snacking. We then get up to pay and I believe it was a manager on duty helped ring it all up and I paid the bill. Sometimes I keep things to myself when I think I could be wrong..  but not this time because I felt like it could make a difference in case someone else wasn't expecting a ton of cheese all over this tasty seafood. I pointed out the menu to him and said it doesn't say these dishes have cheese as an ingredient and my wife disliked her plate. He looked very surprised and insisted it in fact does say it does. I wasn't trying to argue but merely suggest the wait-staff should notify customers that in fact there is a ton of cheese not just on the Pineapple but also in the molcajete. He wasn't willing to see what the menu actually said and I dropped it and said hey you don't need to hear what I'm saying but its your choice to satisfy your customers. I would have easily given a 5 star review... there is no 4.5 stars so 4 it is... I will be going back but now I know I need to request that an ingredient not be added that was never supposed to be there in the first place... ok that's my review... I still love you Puerto Azul.. just work on your people skills... awesome waitress by the way. I didn't catch her name. Also a small detail makes a difference.... <Time>1602563612425<//Time><resp>None< /resp><Rate>4<//Rate><Text>Evening Visit
Since the re-opening of outdoor dining, I would say food is 3.5. I order the cheese enchiladas and the cheese inside wasn't completely melted, we also ordered a molcajete and the meat was a bit dry, however, flavor was pretty good. Longer wait times from the time you order to the time your food is on the table.  Customer service is a 3.5, not sure if its because they are overwhelmed.  BE AWARE:  They charge 3.5% fee to your bill when you pay with your credit/debit card.  We noticed an increase on our bill and asked if the tip was automatically added. This was never mentioned when we were presented our bill nor do they have any signs posted anywhere. If you plan on dining there, bring cash with you to avoid this fee.  Some parking available on the street and at the back.  Some of their parking lot is being used up for outdoor dining set up.  Mask required when you walk to your table, when you leave, and restroom use. All waiters were wearing masks and gloves. They are definitely following safety protocols.< /Text>< username>

<rate>4< /rate>< review>
It's been about 9 years since we last went and we still like the food.  Favorites are the crunch taco, street tacos, burrito and the Mocajete dishes and especially the Mocajete de Mariscos (seafood in a stone bowl).  My kids like the cheese quesadilla which is pretty standard.  They have beer, alcohol and live music on the weekends so it can get busy.  Service is good but wait for check can take some time if they are busy. Inside and outside seating.  The shared parking lot can we difficult to get a spot on the weekends.  Will be back again the next time we are in town.< /review>
